Consulate General of India in New York, Shanti Fund and State University of New York (SUNY) Old Westbury collaborated on the idea of having a “Gandhi Peace Garden”. SUNY Old Westbury contributed to this initiative by donating land for this cause. Keeping in mind the shared democratic values between India and US and spreading the message of the Mahatma in the United States, 150 trees representing the 50 states of the United States are planted at the site. In the Gandhian spirit the trees have been adopted by individuals and organizations in memory of their loved ones. The entire project has been financed in a democratic manner without any financial support from the government. This project exemplifies India's philosophy of living in harmony with nature and would also motivate the diaspora and the university students to study India and the Mahatma. Gandhi Peace Garden was inaugurated by Mr. Narendra Modi, Prime Minister of India on September 24, 2019. https://youtu.be/4k6GyTGlz5I #Gandhi150 #Bapu150 #MahatmaGandhi #IndianConsulate Shades of Red Shirt 2019 American Indian Heritage Day in Texas Celebration Shirt . . . . . . . . . . . . Fancy dance, Pan-Indian dancing, Fancy Feather or Fancy War Dance is a style of dance some believe was originally created by members of the Ponca tribe in the 1920s and 1930s, in an attempt to preserve their culture and religion. It is loosely based on the War dance. Fancy dance was considered appropriate to be performed for visitors to reservations and at \"Wild West\" shows. But today, fancy dancers can be seen at many powwows across the nation and even the world.  In the early history of the Hethuska, the focus of the members of the society was on warfare. Focus on the honors members earned through warfare while defending the tribe from it’s enemies; preserving the acts of valor and heroism of it’s members in song and pantomime dance; and caring for the widows and orphans of fallen warriors. As a society, the structure of the Hethuska was based more on the officers or positions of responsibility needed on the battlefield, which then carried over to positions of responsibility during the dance ceremony.
